# Claude Code - subagents/agent-a7fb69f956b9d6f8f

**Source**: claude-code/subagents/agent-a7fb69f956b9d6f8f.jsonl

---

## USER (2026-07-21 08:03:55)

I need to design a migration plan for upgrading a neuron/Trainium serving layer from vllm-neuron 0.5.0 (NxD Inference based) to v0.21.0.1.0.0 (no NxD dependency, model implementations in-plugin).

## Current Architecture (on a single trn2.48xlarge, 64 NeuronCores)

### Models served:
1. **Tongyi-DeepResearch-30B-A3B** (30B MoE, 3B active) - planning agent
2. **Qwen3-32B** - LLM judge
3. **Qwen3-Embedding-8B** - embedding (uses optimum-neuron, not vLLM)

### Current topology:
- 7 Tongyi replicas at TP=8 (cores 0-55), ports 6008-6014, or 3 replicas at TP=16 (cores 0-47)
- 1 Embedding at TP=8 (cores 56-63), port 6030
- 16 Judge replicas at TP=4 (all 64 cores), ports 8032-8047 (runs after planning, never concurrent)

### Key files to modify:
- `.deps/vllm-neuron/` - vendored plugin (currently 0.5.0)
- `bash/neuron/serve_vllm_neuron.bash` - generic vLLM launcher (sets VLLM_NEURON_FRAMEWORK=neuronx-distributed-inference)
- `bash/neuron/serve_tongyi.bash` - Tongyi model config
- `bash/neuron/serve_tongyi_cluster.bash` - multi-replica cluster with NUMA, supervisors
- `bash/neuron/serve_qwen3_32b_judge.bash` / `serve_qwen3_32b_judge_cluster.bash`
- `bash/neuron/compile_tongyi.bash` - compilation with systemd scope, flock, artifact caching
- `bash/neuron/compile_tongyi_tp16.bash`, `compile_tongyi_tp8_s1.bash`
- `bash/neuron/compile_qwen3_32b_judge.bash`
- `bash/neuron/compile_qwen3_embedding.bash` - uses optimum-cli export
- `bash/neuron/n_tongyi.bash` - end-to-end orchestrator
- `search_agent/neuron_vllm_launcher.py` - monkey-patches NxD's ModelBuilder thread pool, compile-only mode, KV quant dtype
- `search_agent/neuron_embedding_server.py` - FastAPI embedding server
- `search_agent/planning_endpoint_pool.py` - thread-safe endpoint pool with restart coordination
- `tests/test_neuron_vllm_launcher.py`, `tests/test_neuron_throughput.py`

### What the current launcher does that's NxD-specific:
1. Sets `VLLM_NEURON_FRAMEWORK=neuronx-distributed-inference`
2. Monkey-patches `neuronx_distributed.trace.model_builder.concurrent` to limit compile threads
3. Hooks `vllm_neuron.worker.neuronx_distributed_model_loader.NeuronModelBase._compile_and_load_model` for compile-only mode
4. Passes `override_neuron_config` with NxD-specific settings (save_sharded_checkpoint, blockwise_matmul_config, etc.)
5. Bucket configuration via override_neuron_config (context_encoding_buckets, prefix_buckets, token_generation_buckets)

### What vllm-neuron v0.21.0.1.0.0 offers:
- No NxD Inference dependency (model code lives in the plugin)
- Targets vLLM 0.21.0 (major jump from 0.16.0)
- Plugin registered via `vllm.platform_plugins` entry point
- New features: disaggregated inference, segmented prefill (128K), EAGLE3, MXFP4, torch.compile with XLA
- **Currently only supports GPT-OSS 20B/120B and Qwen3-VL 32B** - this is a BETA
- Installation: `pip install --extra-index-url=https://pip.repos.neuron.amazonaws.com -e .` from the cloned repo
- Still uses `python -m vllm.entrypoints.openai.api_server` for serving
- Configuration still via `--additional-config` with `override_neuron_config`

### Critical concern:
The user's primary models (Tongyi-DeepResearch-30B-A3B MoE, Qwen3-32B dense) are NOT listed in v0.21.0.1.0.0's supported models. Only GPT-OSS and Qwen3-VL are supported. The user wants to "推倒重来" (rebuild from scratch) to adapt to the new approach.

### What I need from you:
Design a migration plan that:
1. Addresses the model support gap (do we need to add model support to the plugin? or wait? or use 0.5.3 for some models and 0.21.0 for others?)
2. Outlines what changes in the compile/serve scripts
3. Identifies what from neuron_vllm_launcher.py can be removed (NxD patches no longer needed) vs what needs reimplementation
4. Proposes new topology leveraging disaggregated inference and segmented prefill
5. Keeps the endpoint pool and cluster management patterns that still make sense
6. Considers a phased approach (maybe GPT-OSS first since it's supported, then add model support)

The user also has `serve_gpt_oss_20b.bash` and `serve_gpt_oss_120b.bash` already referenced in their docs, suggesting they may already be exploring GPT-OSS models as alternatives or additions.

Think about what's realistic given model support constraints, and propose the most practical path forward.

@contextmanager\n120\t    def _reordered(self, input_block_ids: torch.Tensor, **inputs):\n121\t        """\n122\t        Context manager that yields reordered input_block_ids, inputs, and a restore         sort_elapsed = (time.perf_counter() - sort_start) * 1000\n134\t            logger.debug("[PERF]       torch.sort: %.2fms", sort_elapsed)\n135\t\n136\t            sort_inputs_start =      logger.debug("[PERF]       _sort_inputs: %.2fms", sort_inputs_elapsed)\n140\t\n141\t            def restore(output: torch.Tensor) -> torch.Tensor:\n142\t                if sorted_ids.shape[0] != Auto-detect from draft checkpoint\'s config.json `architectures` field\n305\t            2. Fallback to target model class if detection fails (homogeneous speculation)\n306\t\n307\t        Args:\n308\t            config: The target model\'s NxDI config (will be modified in place\n309\t                    to attach `fused_spec_config`).\n310\t            neuron_config_dict: Original neuron configuration dictionary from\n311\t                    vLLM\'s `override_neuron_config` (used to extract draft settings).\n312\t            neuronx_model_cls: The NxDI model class for the target model, providing\n313\t                    config loaders. Used as draft class if auto-detection fails.\n314\t            speculative_config: vLLM\'s `SpeculativeConfig` describing the draft\n315\t                    model path and speculation parameters.\n316\t            draft_overrides: Optional dict of draft-specific config overrides applied\n317\t                    as attributes. Use to specify architecture differences (e.g.,\n318\t                    `{"padded_intermediate_size": 14336, "mlp_kernel_enabled": True}`).\n319\t                    Only specify fields that differ from target.\n320\t\n321\t        Raises:\n322\t            ValueError: If draft config cannot be loaded from checkpoint.\n323\t\n324\t        Notes:\n325\t            Only the *target* model should have\n326\t            `neuron_config.enable_fused_speculation=True`. The draft must not,\n327\t            otherwise NxDI would attempt to compile nested fused speculation.\n328\t\n329\t            Configuration inheritance: Draft inherits ALL target fields via deep copy,\n330\t            then selectively overrides specific fields via `draft_overrides`.\n331\t        """\n332\t        # ===== KEY: Deep copy the CREATED target neuron_config object =====\n333\t        # This preserves all target-specific fields without needing to filter\n334\t        draft_neuron_config = copy.deepcopy(config.neuron_config)\n335\t\n336\t        # Modify specific draft attributes (reference pattern)\n337\t        if not getattr(config.neuron_config, "enable_eagle_speculation", False):\n338\t            draft_neuron_config.speculation_length = 0\n339\t\n340\t        draft_neuron_config.enable_fused_speculation = False\n341\t\n342\t        if getattr(config.neuron_config, "draft_model_modules_to_not_convert", None):\n343\t            draft_neuron_config.modules_to_not_convert = (\n344\t                config.neuron_config.draft_model_modules_to_not_convert\n345\t            )\n346\t\n347\t        if getattr(config.neuron_config, "enable_eagle_speculation", False):\n348\t            draft_neuron_config.is_eagle_draft = True\n349\t\n350\t        # Apply draft overrides as attributes (not dict update)\n351\t        if draft_overrides:\n352\t            for key, value in draft_overrides.items():\n353\t                setattr(draft_neuron_config, key, value)\n354\t\n355\t        # ===== Load draft config for architecture inspection =====\n356\t        logger.info("Inspecting draft model config from: %s", speculative_config.model)\n357\t        try:\n358\t            from transformers import AutoConfig\n359\t\n360\t            draft_hf_config_for_inspection = AutoConfig.from_pretrained(\n361\t                speculative_config.model, trust_remote_code=False\n362\t            )\n363\t            logger.debug(\n364\t                "Draft config architectures: %s",\n365\t                getattr(draft_hf_config_for_inspection, "architectures", None),\n366\t            )\n367\t        except Exception as e:\n368\t            logger.error("Failed to load draft config for inspection: %s", e)\n369\t            raise ValueError(\n370\t                f"Cannot load draft model config from \'{speculative_config.model}\'. "\n371\t                f"Please ensure the path is correct and config.json exists. "\n372\t                f"Error: {e}"\n373\t            ) from e\n374\t\n375\t        # ===== Auto-detect draft model class =====\n376\t        draft_neuron_model_cls = None\n377\t        auto_detected_cls = None\n378\t\n379\t        draft_arch = (\n380\t            draft_hf_config_for_inspection.architectures[0]\n381\t            if hasattr(draft_hf_config_for_inspection, "architectures")\n382\t            and draft_hf_config_for_inspection.architectures\n383\t            else None\n384\t        )\n385\t\n386\t        # Check for user-provided draft_neuron_model_class override\n387\t        draft_class_override = None\n388\t        if draft_overrides and "draft_neuron_model_class" in draft_overrides:\n389\t            draft_class_override = draft_overrides.pop("draft_neuron_model_class")\n390\t            logger.info(\n391\t                "User provided draft_neuron_model_class override: \'%s\'",\n392\t                draft_class_override,\n393\t            )\n394\t\n395\t        if draft_arch:\n396\t            logger.info(\n397\t                "Auto-detected draft architecture from config.json: %s", draft_arch\n398\t            )\n399\t            try:\n400\t                auto_detected_cls = _get_neuron_model_cls(draft_arch)\n401\t                logger.info(\n402\t                    "Auto-detected Neuron model class: %s",\n403\t                    auto_detected_cls.__name__,\n404\t                )\n405\t            except ValueError as e:\n406\t                logger.warning(\n407\t                    "Draft architecture \'%s\' is not supported on Neuron. Error: %s",\n408\t                    draft_arch,\n409\t                    e,\n410\t                )\n411\t        else:\n412\t            logger.warning(\n413\t                "No \'architectures\' field found in draft config at %s.",\n414\t                speculative_config.model,\n415\t            )\n416\t\n417\t        # Resolve final draft model class: override > auto-detected > fallback\n418\t        if draft_class_override:\n419\t            try:\n420\t                draft_neuron_model_cls = _get_neuron_model_cls(draft_class_override)\n421\t                if auto_detected_cls:\n422\t                    logger.info(\n423\t                        "Using OVERRIDE class \'%s\' (auto-detected was \'%s\')",\n424\t                        draft_neuron_model_cls.__name__,\n425\t                        auto_detected_cls.__name__,\n426\t                    )\n427\t                else:\n428\t                    logger.info(\n429\t                        "Using OVERRIDE class \'%s\'",\n430\t                        draft_neuron_model_cls.__name__,\n431\t                    )\n432\t            except ValueError as e:\n433\t                logger.warning(\n434\t                    "Override class \'%s\' not found: %s. Falling back.",\n435\t                    draft_class_override,\n436\t                    e,\n437\t                )\n438\t                draft_neuron_model_cls = auto_detected_cls\n439\t        else:\n440\t            draft_neuron_model_cls = auto_detected_cls\n441\t\n442\t        # Fallback to target class if still None\n443\t        if draft_neuron_model_cls is None:\n444\t            draft_neuron_model_cls = neuronx_model_cls\n445\t            logger.info(\n446\t                "Falling back to target model class for draft: %s",\n447\t                draft_neuron_model_cls.__name__,\n448\t            )\n449\t\n450\t        # ===== Create draft config using load_pretrained_config (CALLABLE) =====\n451\t        logger.info(\n452\t            "Creating draft config with class: %s", draft_neuron_model_cls.__name__\n453\t        )\n454\t\n455\t        draft_config = draft_neuron_model_cls.get_config_cls()(\n456\t            draft_neuron_config,\n457\t            load_config=load_pretrained_config(speculative_config.model),\n458\t        )\n459\t\n460\t        # ===== Create and attach fused spec config =====\n461\t        fused_spec_config = FusedSpecNeuronConfig(\n462\t            neuronx_model_cls._model_cls,\n463\t            draft_config=draft_config,\n464\t            draft_model_path=speculative_config.model,\n465\t            draft_model_cls=draft_neuron_model_cls,\n466\t        )\n467\t\n468\t        config.fused_spec_config = fused_spec_config\n469\t        logger.info("Fused speculation config initialized successfully")\n470\t\n471\t\n472\tclass NeuronCausalLM(NeuronModelBase):\n473\t    def _remask_fused_spec_output(self, fused, inputs):\n474\t        """\n475\t        Handle NxDI fused speculation output.\n476\t\n477\t        NxDI fused spec returns:\n478\t        fused[0] = accepted_tokens_with_padding : [B, T], 0-padded\n479\t        fused[-1] = next_pos_ids\n480\t\n481\t        We convert the 0-padding to -1 past the number of tokens actually\n482\t        generated in this step, so the runner can strip pads.\n483\t        """\n484\t        start_time = time.perf_counter()\n485\t\n486\t        accepted_tokens_with_padding = fused[0]\n487\t        next_pos_ids = fused[-1].squeeze(-1)  # [B]\n488\t        positions_vec = inputs["position_ids"][:, -1].to(next_pos_ids.device)\n489\t\n490\t        # Number of tokens generated this step\n491\t        generated_token_counts = (next_pos_ids - positions_vec).to(torch.long)\n492\t\n493\t        # Mask tail with -1 so runner can strip pads\n494\t        B, T = accepted_tokens_with_padding.shape\n495\t        generated_token_counts = generated_token_counts.clamp_(0, T)\n496\t\n497\t        masked = accepted_tokens_with_padding.clone()\n498\t        for b in range(B):\n499\t            masked[b, generated_token_counts[b] :] = -1\n500\t\n501\t        elapsed_ms = (time.perf_counter() - start_time) * 1000\n502\t        logger.debug(\n503\t            "[PERF]     _remask_fused_spec_output: %.2fms [batch=%d]", elapsed_ms, B\n504\t        )\n505\t\n506\t        return masked\n507\t\n508\t    def forward(self, input_ids, input_block_ids, **kwargs):\n509\t        forward_start = time.perf_counter()\n510\t        batch_size = (\n511\t            input_ids.shape[0]\n512\t            if isinstance(input_ids, torch.Tensor)\n513\t            else len(input_ids)\n514\t        )\n515\t\n516\t        with self._reordered(input_block_ids, input_ids=input_ids, **kwargs) as (\n517\t            sorted_ids,\n518\t            inputs,\n519\t            restore,\n520\t        ):\n521\t            # Time model execution\n522\t            model_start = time.perf_counter()\n523\t            output = self.model(\n524\t                inputs["input_ids"],\n525\t                attention_mask=None,\n526\t                seq_ids=sorted_ids,\n527\t                block_table=inputs["block_tables"],\n528\t                **{\n529\t                    k: v\n530\t                    for k, v in inputs.items()\n531\t                    if k\n532\t                    not in ["input_ids", "block_tables", "prefill_completion_state"]\n533\t                },\n534\t            )\n535\t            model_elapsed = (time.perf_counter() - model_start) * 1000\n536\t            logger.debug("[PERF]     model_execution: %.2fms", model_elapsed)\n537\t\n538\t            # Time output processing\n539\t            output_proc_start = time.perf_counter()\n540\t            if self.model.config.neuron_config.on_device_sampling_config:\n541\t                output = output.hidden_states\n542\t                if getattr(\n543\t                    self.model.config.neuron_config, "enable_fused_speculation", False\n544\t                ):\n545\t                    fused = output\n546\t                    output = self._remask_fused_spec_output(fused, inputs)\n547\t            else:\n548\t                if self.neuron_config.is_chunked_prefill:\n549\t                    assert kwargs.get("prefill_completion_state") is not None\n550\t                    idx_for_sampling = (\n551\t                        kwargs["prefill_completion_state"].nonzero().flatten()\n552\t                    )\n553\t                    output = output.logits[0, idx_for_sampling, :]\n554\t                else:\n555\t                    output = output.logits[:, -1, :]\n556\t            output_proc_elapsed = (time.perf_counter() - output_proc_start) * 1000\n557\t            logger.debug("[PERF]     output_processing: %.2fms", output_proc_elapsed)\n558\t\n559\t            # Time restore operation\n560\t            restore_start = time.perf_counter()\n561\t            result = restore(output)\n562\t            restore_elapsed = (time.perf_counter() - restore_start) * 1000\n563\t            logger.debug("[PERF]     restore: %.2fms", restore_elapsed)\n564\t\n565\t            forward_elapsed = (time.perf_counter() - forward_start) * 1000\n566\t            logger.debug(\n567\t                "[PERF]   forward() total: %.2fms [batch=%d]",\n568\t                forward_elapsed,\n569\t                batch_size,\n570\t            )\n571\t\n572\t            return result\n573\t\n574\t    def sample(self, logits: torch.Tensor) -> SamplerOutput | None:\n575\t        if self.model.config.neuron_config.on_device_sampling_config:\n576\t            return SamplerOutput(\n577\t                # The sampled tokens are expanded to 2D tensor with shape\n578\t                # [num_requests, 1], where each row represents one generated\n579\t                # token per request.\n580\t                sampled_token_ids=logits.unsqueeze(-1),\n581\t                logprobs_tensors=None,\n582\t            )\n583\t        else:\n584\t            # CPU sampling is now handled by the model runner\n585\t            # This should not be called when on_device_sampling_config is None\n586\t            # as the model runner will use its own CPU sampler\n587\t            raise RuntimeError(\n588\t                "CPU sampling should be handled by the model runner, not the model. "\n589\t                "This indicates a bug in the sampling path routing."\n590\t            )\n591\t\n592\t    def load_weights(self, model_name_or_path: str, architecture: str, **kwargs):\n593\t        neuronx_model_cls = _get_neuron_model_cls(architecture)\n594\t        success, compiled_model_path, config = self._load_weights_common(\n595\t            model_name_or_path, neuronx_model_cls, **kwargs\n596\t        )\n597\t\n598\t        if not success:\n599\t            if not os.path.exists(model_name_or_path):\n600\t                model_name_or_path = self._save_pretrained_model(model_name_or_path)\n601\t            self._compile_and_load_model(\n602\t                model_name_or_path, neuronx_model_cls, config, compiled_model_path\n603\t            )\n604\t        return success, compiled_model_path\n605\t\n606\t\n607\tclass NeuronMultiModalCausalLM(NeuronCausalLM):\n608\t    def load_weights(self, model_name_or_path: str, architecture: str, **kwargs):\n609\t        neuronx_model_cls = _get_neuron_model_cls(architecture)\n610\t\n611\t        # Neuron ImageToText model configs have nested text and vision config\n612\t        # each has their own neuron_config.     Neuron model class\n968\t\n969\t    Examples:\n970\t        _get_neuron_model_cls("LlamaForCausalLM")\n971\t        <class \'NeuronLlamaForCausalLM\'>\n972\t\n973\t Patch accelerator stream/device APIs for CPU mode to prevent CUDA fallthrough\n    if envs.VLLM_NEURON_CPU_MODE:\n        torch.accelerator.current_stream = lambda device=None: type(\n            "_S", (), {"device": torch.device("cpu")}\n        )()\n        torch.accelerator.current_device_index = lambda: 0\n\n\ntry:\n    _init_backend()\nexcept (ImportError, KeyError):\n    pass\n\n# Import-time so it survives spawn-mode re-imports (EngineCore subprocess\n# never calls check_and_update_config).\nfrom vllm_neuron.vllm.patches.port_hold_patch import apply_port_hold_patch\n\napply_port_hold_patch()\n\n\ndef register():\n    """Register the Neuron platform if Neuron devices are present, else return None.\n\n    The backend is selected based on the VLLM_NEURON_BACKEND environment variable:\n    - "vllm_neuron": Use the vLLM Neuron backend (default)\n    - "neuron_native": Use the neuron native backend\n\n    If VLLM_NEURON_BACKEND is not set, defaults to vllm_neuron.\n    """\n    if not _is_cpu_mode() and not _is_cpu_compile() and not _is_neuron_dev():\n        warnings.warn(\n            "No Neuron devices found. It extends [vLLM](https://docs.vllm.ai/) with a Neuron backend, providing the same vLLM APIs and configuration you are already familiar with.\n\n> **If you are using vLLM with NxD Inference (0.5.x plugin version),** see the [release-0.5.3 branch](https://github.com/aws-neuron/private-vllm-neuron/tree/release-0.5.3) and the [NxD Inference + vLLM documentation](https://awsdocs-neuron.readthedocs-hosted.com/en/latest/libraries/nxd-inference/index.html). To migrate to the plugin based on 0.21.0+, see the [migration guide](docs/getting-started/migration-nxdi-to-vllm-neuron.md).\n\n## Installation\n\n```bash\ngit clone -b release-0.21.0.1.0.0 https://github.com/vllm-project/vllm-neuron.git\ncd vllm-neuron\npip install --extra-index-url=https://pip.repos.neuron.amazonaws.com -e .\n```\n\nThis installs the vLLM Neuron plugin from source along with vLLM and the required Neuron SDK packages. See [Version](#version) for the full compatibility matrix.\n\n**For detailed environment setup and instance selection**: See the [Setup guide](docs/getting-started/setup-guide.md).\n\n## Quick Start\n\nRun the following command from a shell terminal in the local or instance environment (`vllm` must be in the path) where vLLM is configured:\n\n```bash\nvllm serve openai/gpt-oss-20b \\\n    --tensor-parallel-size 8 \\\n    --max-model-len 8192 \\\n    --max-num-batched-tokens 4096 \\\n    --max-num-seqs 4\n```\n\n## Supported Models\n\nModels listed below are tested end-to-end on Neuron hardware with correctness validation and performance benchmarking.\n\n| Family | Model | Type | Instance | Correctness | Perf Test | Perf Tuning |\n|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|\n| GPT-OSS | 20B, 120B | Text | Trn2, Trn3 | ✅ | ✅ | In progress |\n| Qwen3-VL | 32B (Dense) | Multimodal | Trn2, Trn3 | ✅ | ✅ | In progress |\n\n- **Correctness** — Accuracy validation passing (logit comparison, dataset accuracy validation)\n- **Perf Test** — Performance benchmark tests tracked across releases\n- **Perf Tuning** — Active optimization work being done\n\n> **Note:** This list includes only the models currently supported in the latest plugin version and does not include models under development or on roadmap.\n\nPerformance improvements are delivered incrementally with each Neuron release.\n\n## Features\n\nFeature support is at the framework level. See the model cards in [`docs/model-recipes/`](docs/model-recipes/) for per-model feature availability and the [features guide](docs/guides/features-guide.md) for configuration details.\n\n| Category | Feature | Status |\n|---|---|---|\n| **Serving** | Continuous batching | ✅ |\n| | OpenAI-compatible APIs | ✅ |\n| | Streaming | ✅ |\n| | Structured outputs (JSON, regex, grammar) | ✅ |\n| | Tool calling | ✅ |\n| | LoRA adapters | ❌ |\n| | Weight reload API | ❌ |\n| | Sleep mode (sleep/wake_up API) | ❌ |\n| **Parallelism** | Tensor parallelism (TP) | ✅ |\n| | Sequence parallelism (SP) | ✅ |\n| | Data parallelism (DP) | ✅ |\n| | Expert parallelism (EP) | ✅ |\n| | Vision encoder parallelism | ✅ |\n| | Pipeline parallelism (PP) | ❌ |\n| | Context parallelism (CP) | ❌ |\n| **Performance** | Paged KV cache | ✅ |\n| | Prefix caching | ✅ |\n| | Segmented prefill | ✅ |\n| | Chunked prefill (mixed batching) | ❌ |\n| | Disaggregated inference (1P1D, xPyD) | ✅ |\n| | Async scheduling | ✅ |\n| | On-device sampling (top-k, top-p, temperature) | ✅ |\n| | KV cache offloading | ❌ |\n| | Disaggregated encoder | ❌ |\n| **Compilation** | torch.compile (XLA backend) | ✅ |\n| | torch.compile (native PyTorch) | ❌ |\n| | Compile cache (local/remote) | ✅ |\n| | CPU compilation | ✅ |\n| **Speculative Decoding** | EAGLE3 | ✅ |\n| | MTP | ❌ |\n| **Quantization** | BF16 | ✅ |\n| | FP8 | ✅ |\n| | Quantized KV cache (FP8) | ✅ |\n| | MXFP4 weights (Trn3) | ✅ |\n| | MXFP8 weights (Trn3) | ❌ |\n| **Multimodal Inputs** | Images + text | ✅ |\n| | Videos + text | ✅ |\n| | Audio | ❌ |\n| **Observability** | Production metrics (`/metrics` endpoint) | ✅ |\n| | Profiler API | ✅ |\n\n**Status legend:**\n\n- ✅ Supported — integrated and tested for at least one model\n- ❌ Not supported — may be considered for future releases\n\n## Documentation\n\nFull documentation sources are found in [`docs/`](docs/). These docs are published to [awsdocs-neuron.readthedocs-hosted.com/en/latest/vllm-neuron](https://awsdocs-neuron.readthedocs-hosted.com/en/latest/vllm-neuron/docs/index.html).\n\n**Deploying supported models:**\n\n| Folder | What's inside |\n|---|---|\n| [`docs/getting-started/`](docs/getting-started/) | Setup, quickstarts, migration from NxD Inference |\n| [`docs/guides/`](docs/guides/) | Features guide, configuration reference, metrics, profiling |\n| [`docs/model-recipes/`](docs/model-recipes/) | Per-model deployment recipes |\n| [`docs/tutorials/`](docs/tutorials/) | End-to-end walkthroughs (DI, prefix caching, etc.) |\n\n**Implementing new models & optimizing performance:**\n\n| Folder | What's inside |\n|---|---|\n| [`docs/model-dev/`](docs/model-dev/) | Model onboarding, CPU development, etc. |\n| [`docs/design/`](docs/design/) | Architecture deep dives (parallelism, DI, prefix caching, etc.) |\n\n## Version", 'is_error': False}]

[{'tool_use_id': 'toolu_bdrk_01TjVQWpR6ZsfeyHfgvJvitT', 'type': 'tool_result', 'content': '# How to migrate from NxD Inference to vLLM Neuron\n\n<!-- meta: description: Migration guide covering the practitioner flow and\nperformance engineer flow for moving from NxDI to vLLM Neuron. -->\n<!-- meta: date_updated: 2026-07-15 -->\n<!-- Content type: procedural-how-to -->\n<!-- Jira: NDOC-190 -->\n\n## Task overview\n\nFollow this guide when moving from the legacy NxD Inference integration to the\nvLLM Neuron plugin. Migration covers two distinct paths, each documented as its\nown sub-guide below:\n\n- **[Migrate a deployment](#guide-1-migrate-a-deployment)** — for ML\n  practitioners and performance engineers moving an existing NxDI deployment of\n  a supported model to the plugin: mapping server flags and `neuron_config`,\n  validating accuracy, and benchmarking.\n- **[Migrate a custom model](#guide-2-migrate-a-custom-model)** — for teams who\n  authored a custom model architecture against NxDI and need to re-implement it\n  on the vLLM Neuron plugin\'s building blocks.\n\nStart with the deployment guide if you serve a model that vLLM Neuron already\nsupports. Use the custom-model guide if you maintain your own modeling code.\n\n## Prerequisites\n\n- Existing NxD Inference deployment (using `neuronx-distributed-inference`\n  with the legacy vLLM Neuron component)\n- A new Trainium/Inferentia instance with the vLLM Neuron plugin installed (see\n  [setup guide](setup-guide.md))\n- Access to the same model weights for comparison testing\n\n## Guide 1: Migrate a deployment\n\nUse this path when vLLM Neuron already supports your model and you are moving an\nexisting NxDI serving deployment to the plugin.\n\n### 1. Assess migration scope\n\nDetermine which features of NxDI your deployment uses:\n\n| NxDI Feature                    | vLLM Neuron                              | Notes                                   |\n| ---------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------- |\n| Continuous batching                | Enabled by default                                  | No configuration needed                 |\n| Prefix caching                     | Enabled by default                              | No configuration needed     |\n| Speculative decoding | EAGLE3 only, via `--speculative-config`               | Vanilla draft-model speculative decoding is not supported; migrate to an EAGLE3 draft            |\n| Disaggregated inference            | Supported (1P1D, xPyD)                              | Topology configuration changed          |\n| Quantization (INT8/FP8)            | `quantized` + `quantization_dtype` in neuron_config | Same quantization approach              |\n| On-device sampling                 | Enabled by default                                  | Supports temperature, top_k, top_p      |\n| Sequence parallelism                 | Enabled by default                                  | No configuration needed      |\n| Data parallelism                 | Native vLLM data parallel support                                  | Server configuration changed     |\n| Expert parallelism                 | Native vLLM expert parallel support                                 | Server configuration changed      |\n| Decode bucketing                 | vLLM Neuron buckets decode by num_seqs by default. Decode context length bucketing is supported via `decode_context_length_buckets`      | Server configuration changed      |\n\n### 2. Map API and parameters\n\n**Server startup:**\n\n```bash\n# NxDI (legacy vLLM Neuron integration)\nVLLM_NEURON_FRAMEWORK=\'neuronx-distributed-inference\' \\\npython3 -m vllm.entrypoints.openai.api_server \\\n    --model meta-llama/Llama-3.3-70B-Instruct \\\n    --device neuron \\\n    --tensor-parallel-size 32 \\\n    --max-num-seqs 8 \\\n    --max-model-len 4096 \\\n    --override-neuron-config \'{"on_device_sampling_config": {"dynamic": true}}\'\n\n# vLLM Neuron plugin (new)\nexport VLLM_NEURON_COMPILATION_TIMEOUT=1200\nexport VLLM_EXECUTE_MODEL_TIMEOUT_SECONDS=1200\nvllm serve openai/gpt-oss-20b \\\n    --tensor-parallel-size 8 \\\n    --max-model-len 4096 \\\n    --max-num-batched-tokens 2048 \\\n    --max-num-seqs 4 \\\n    --hf-overrides \'{"quantization_config": {}}\' \\\n    --additional-config \'{\n      "neuron_config": {\n        "on_device_sampling_config": {}\n      }\n    }\'\n```\n\nKey differences:\n\n- No `--device neuron` flag needed — the plugin auto-detects Neuron hardware\n- No `VLLM_NEURON_FRAMEWORK` environment variable needed — the plugin registers\n  itself with vLLM via its entry point\n- Neuron-specific settings move from `--override-neuron-config` to\n  `--additional-config`, nested under `neuron_config` (see below)\n\n**Configuration override:**\n\n```bash\n# NxDI: flat neuron config via --override-neuron-config\n--override-neuron-config \'{"context_encoding_buckets": [128, 256, 512, 1024]}\'\n\n# vLLM Neuron: nested under additional_config, with renamed fields\n--additional-config \'{"neuron_config": {"num_batched_tokens_buckets": [128, 256, 512, 1024]}}\'\n```\n\nField names also changed — for example, NxDI\'s `context_encoding_buckets`\nmaps to `num_batched_tokens_buckets`. See the\n[configuration reference](../guides/reference-configuration.md) for the full\nlist of `neuron_config` options.\n\n### 3. Migrate deployment configuration\n\n1. Update your server launch command using the parameter mapping above\n2. Remove `--device neuron`, the `VLLM_NEURON_FRAMEWORK` environment variable,\n   and any other NxDI-specific flags\n3. Move any `--override-neuron-config` settings under `--additional-config`,\n   nested inside `neuron_config`, renaming fields as needed (for example,\n   `context_encoding_buckets` → `num_batched_tokens_buckets`)\n4. Drop `--num-gpu-blocks-override` and `--block-size` unless you were using\n   them for advanced tuning — the plugin sizes the KV cache automatically\n\nTo learn how to enable and tune vLLM Neuron features (bucketing, prefix\ncaching, quantization, disaggregated inference, and more) in your new\ndeployment, see the [features guide](../guides/features-guide.md).\n\n### 4. Validate output accuracy\n\nRun the same prompts through both deployments and validate that results are comparable.\nUse datasets or logit validation to evaluate accuracy.\n\nIf the model is inaccurate, see the\n[accuracy debugging guide](../model-dev/accuracy-debugging-guide.md).\n\n### 5. Benchmark performance\n\nCompare latency and throughput between deployments:\n\n- **TTFT** (time to first token): Should be comparable or improved with prefix\n  caching\n- **ITL** (inter-token latency): Should be comparable or improved\n- **Throughput** (tokens/sec): Should be comparable at the same batch size\n\n### 6. Staged rollout\n\n1. Deploy vLLM Neuron alongside the existing NxDI deployment\n2. Route a small percentage of traffic to the new deployment\n3. Monitor accuracy metrics and latency SLAs\n4. Gradually increase traffic to the new deployment\n5. Decommission the NxDI deployment once validated\n\n### Confirm your work\n\nDeployment migration is successful when:\n\n- Model output accuracy is similar between NxDI and vLLM Neuron for your test\n  prompts\n- Latency (TTFT, ITL) meets your SLA requirements\n- Throughput matches or exceeds the NxDI deployment\n- All required features (quantization, prefix caching, etc.) are functioning\n\n### Common issues\n\n#### Out-of-memory at startup\n\n- **Possible solution**: The plugin sizes the KV cache automatically from\n  available HBM and `--gpu-memory-utilization`; you do not set\n  `--num-gpu-blocks-override` as in some NxDI flows. If the server runs out of\n  memory, reduce `--gpu-memory-utilization`, `--max-num-seqs`, or\n  `--max-model-len`.\n\n#### Performance regression after migration\n\n- **Possible solution**: Verify bucket configurations match your traffic\n  pattern. Reduce `num_batched_tokens_buckets` to match your actual prompt length\n  distribution. Ensure compilation artifacts are cached.\n\n## Guide 2: Migrate a custom model\n\nUse this path when you authored a custom model architecture against NxDI (for\nexample, subclassing NxDI modeling code or `NeuronConfig`) and vLLM Neuron does\nnot yet support it out of the box. On the plugin, you re-implement the model\nusing vLLM Neuron\'s building blocks and register it with vLLM\'s model registry —\nthere is no direct port of NxDI modeling classes.\n\nAt a high level:\n\n1. **Implement the model** against the plugin\'s building blocks (attention, MLP,\n   and parallel layer primitives), applying the plugin\'s tensor-parallel\n   sharding conventions rather than NxDI\'s.\n2. **Register the model** with vLLM\'s model registry so `vllm serve` can resolve\n   your architecture.\n3. **Compile and test** the model on Neuron to confirm it compiles and runs.\n4. **Validate accuracy** against a reference (HuggingFace) implementation.\n5. **Benchmark and tune** performance (bucketing, parallelism, quantization).\n\nThis is a code migration, not a configuration change, so it is documented in\nfull separately. For the complete step-by-step instructions, code patterns, and\nper-component details, follow the\n[model onboarding guide](../model-dev/onboarding-models.md). Once your model is\nonboarded, return to [Guide 1](#guide-1-migrate-a-deployment) to migrate its\nserving deployment.\n\n## Related information\n\n- For supported models and features, see the [README](https://github.com/vllm-project/vllm-neuron#supported-models)\n  and [model cards](../model-recipes/index.md).\n- [Model onboarding guide](../model-dev/onboarding-models.md)\n- [Accuracy debugging guide](../model-dev/accuracy-debugging-guide.md)\n- [Features guide](../guides/features-guide.md)', 'is_error': False}]

## USER (2026-07-21 08:12:14)

[{'tool_use_id': 'toolu_bdrk_01PwKB8EQxaZPnYWEtWZ71gE', 'type': 'tool_result', 'content': '# How to onboard a model to vLLM Neuron\n\n<!-- meta: description: Onboard a new model architecture to vLLM Neuron and\nmake it available for online and offline serving on AWS Trainium and\nInferentia. -->\n<!-- meta: keywords: vLLM, Neuron, model onboarding, custom models, Trainium,\nInferentia, tensor parallelism, KV cache -->\n<!-- meta: date_updated: 2026-06-11 -->\n<!-- Content type: procedural-how-to -->\n<!-- Jira: NDOC-186 -->\n\n## Task overview\n\nThis topic discusses how to onboard a new model architecture so it can be served\nthrough vLLM Neuron. You will implement the model using the vLLM Neuron\nplugin\'s building blocks, register it with vLLM\'s model registry, compile,\nvalidate accuracy, and benchmark performance.\n\n:::{note}\nThe vLLM Neuron plugin implements models directly using `torch_neuronx`, NKI\n(Neuron Kernel Interface) kernels, and its own parallel infrastructure. The\nplugin provides its own functional operators (`vllm_neuron.functional`), neural\nnetwork modules (`vllm_neuron.nn`), weight loading utilities, and parallel state\nmanagement built on top of `torch.distributed` and vLLM\'s distributed primitives.\n:::\n\n:::{note}\nFor models deployed through NxD Inference directly (without vLLM), see the legacy\n[NxDI model onboarding guide](https://awsdocs-neuron.readthedocs-hosted.com/en/latest/libraries/nxd-inference/developer_guides/onboarding-models.html).\n:::\n\n## Prerequisites\n\n- **vLLM Neuron environment**: A working vLLM Neuron setup on a Trainium or\n  Inferentia instance. See [setup guide](../getting-started/setup-guide.md).\n- **A model you want to onboard**: You may be porting from an existing\n  implementation (e.g., Hugging Face Transformers), writing from scratch, or\n  adapting from another framework. Any approach works as long as the result\n  satisfies the runner interface described below.\n- **Familiarity with the plugin codebase**: The\n  [vLLM Neuron plugin source](https://github.com/aws-neuron/vllm-neuron) contains\n  annotated reference implementations (Llama, GPT-OSS) that demonstrate\n  common patterns. These are useful as examples, not mandatory templates.\n\n## End-to-end onboarding flow\n\n```text\n┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│  1. Implement model    2. Register with   3. Compile &   4. Validate      │\n│     (config, layers,      vLLM registry      smoke test     accuracy      │\n│      factory, weights)                                                    │\n│                                                          5. Benchmark     │\n└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n```\n\nThe reference implementations are heavily annotated with\n`# <-- MODEL-SPECIFIC` and `# >>> PARALLELISM <<<` comments to distinguish\nmodel-specific code from reusable parallelism infrastructure. Use the Llama\nimplementation (`vllm_neuron/model/llama3/`) as your primary porting template\nfor dense models, or the GPT-OSS implementation (`vllm_neuron/model/gpt_oss/`)\nfor MoE models.\n\n## Instructions\n\n### 1. Implement the model\n\nCreate a model directory under `src/model/` with the following structure:\n\n```text\nsrc/model/your_model/\n├── __init__.py\n├── config.py          # Model-specific dataclass config\n├── factory.py         # Factory class for vLLM ModelRegistry\n└── model.py           # Full model implementation\n```\n\n#### 1a. Define the model config (`config.py`)\n\nCreate a dataclass that holds the model\'s architecture parameters. Implement a\n`from_configs` classmethod that parses a HuggingFace `PretrainedConfig` into your\nconfig.\n\n```python\nfrom dataclasses import dataclass\nimport torch\nfrom transformers import PretrainedConfig\nfrom vllm_neuron.model.neuron_config import NeuronConfig\n\n@dataclass\nclass YourModelConfig:\n    # Architecture parameters (model-specific)\n    hidden_size: int = 4096\n    num_attention_heads: int = 32\n    num_key_value_heads: int = 8\n    num_hidden_layers: int = 32\n    intermediate_size: int = 14336\n    head_dim: int = 128\n    vocab_size: int = 128256\n    max_position_embeddings: int = 131072\n    rms_norm_eps: float = 1e-5\n    rope_theta: float = 500000.0\n    rope_scaling: dict | None = None\n    tie_word_embeddings: bool = False\n    torch_dtype: torch.dtype = torch.bfloat16\n\n    # Framework config\n    neuron_config: NeuronConfig | None = None\n\n    @classmethod\n    def from_configs(cls, hf_config: PretrainedConfig, neuron_config: NeuronConfig = None):\n        config_dict = hf_config.to_dict()\n        field_names = {f.name for f in cls.__dataclass_fields__.values()}\n        filtered_dict = {k: v for k, v in config_dict.items() if k in field_names}\n        if neuron_config is not None:\n            filtered_dict["neuron_config"] = neuron_config\n        return cls(**filtered_dict)\n```\n\nThe `NeuronConfig` dataclass (provided by the plugin at\n`vllm_neuron.model.neuron_config`) carries Neuron-specific settings: parallelism\ndegrees (`attention_dp_size`, `mlp_dp_size`, `embedding_dp_size`,\n`lm_head_dp_size`, `ep_degree`), on-device sampling config, bucket\nconfigurations, and quantization settings.\n\n#### 1b. Implement model components (`model.py`)\n\nYour model implementation can use any valid PyTorch code that the Neuron compiler\ncan trace. The plugin provides optimized building blocks (functional operators\nbacked by NKI kernels, parallel modules, weight loading utilities) that you can\nuse if they fit your architecture. These are conveniences, not requirements — you\nare free to write your own operators, use different parallelism strategies, or\nstructure your model however you like, as long as the result satisfies the runner\ninterface contract described below.\n\n##### Available building blocks\n\nThe following utilities are provided by the plugin and used by the existing model\nimplementations. They handle common patterns efficiently on Neuron:\n\n| Component | Available utilities |\n| --- | --- |\n| Attention | `vllm_neuron.functional.qkv_proj`, `flash_attention`, `segmented_attention`, `attention_decode`, `o_proj`, `gen_attention_decode_mask` — NKI-backed operators with PyTorch CPU fallbacks for tracing |\n| MLP | `vllm_neuron.functional.mlp` — fused gate/up/down projection with NKI kernel |\n| Embedding | `vllm_neuron.nn.VocabDimShardedEmbedding` — vocab-dimension-sharded embedding with built-in scatter for SP |\n| LM Head | `vllm_neuron.nn.ColumnParallelLinear` — column-parallel linear with optional output gathering |\n| Normalization | Standard `nn.Module` implementations (RMSNorm, LayerNorm) — no special Neuron module needed |\n| Weight loading | `vllm_neuron.utils.weight_loader.sharding_weight_loader`, `fused_qkv_weight_loader`, `with_rank_override` — closure-based loaders for checkpoint → parameter transforms |\n| Collectives | `vllm.distributed.parallel_state.get_tp_group()` — provides `all_gather`, `reduce_scatter`, `all_reduce`; plugin also provides custom group coordinators in `vllm_neuron.parallel.neuron_parallel_state` |\n| KV cache | `vllm_neuron.model.kv_cache.KVSpec`, `LayerSpec` — dataclasses for declaring cache requirements |\n\n:::{note}\nThe functional operators in `vllm_neuron.functional` (imported as `NF`) dispatch\nto NKI kernels when running on Neuron hardware and fall back to equivalent PyTorch\noperations on CPU. This dual-path design allows `torch.compile` to trace the graph\non CPU while the compiled NEFF uses optimized kernels at runtime. You can use\nthese operators, write your own, or mix both.\n:::\n\n##### Understanding the runner → model interface\n\nThe `NeuronModelRunner` orchestrates execution between vLLM\'s scheduler and your\nmodel. Understanding what it passes to `forward()` is essential for implementing a\ncorrect model.\n\n*Forward signature:*\n\nYour top-level model\'s `forward()` receives these keyword arguments (all are\nalways present once torch.compile traces the graph — you cannot conditionally\naccept/reject kwargs between calls):\n\n```python\ndef forward(\n    self,\n    input_ids: torch.LongTensor,         # [total_tokens] — token IDs, padded to bucket size\n    positions: torch.Tensor,             # [total_tokens] — position IDs (int32)\n    attn_metadata: dict,                 # Per-layer attention metadata (see below)\n    sampling_positions: torch.Tensor,    # [num_reqs] — indices into the token dim for LM head\n    sampling_params: torch.Tensor,       # [num_reqs, 3] — [top_k, top_p, temperature] (None if CPU sampling)\n    spec_decode_metadata=None,           # SpecDecodeMetadata for rejection sampling\n    logit_mask: torch.Tensor,            # [num_logit_rows, vocab_size] — grammar/structured output mask\n    rank: torch.Tensor,                  # scalar — TP rank\n    inputs_embeds: torch.Tensor | None = None,   # [total_tokens, hidden_size] (prompt-embeds path)\n    is_token_ids: torch.Tensor | None = None,    # [total_tokens] bool (prompt-embeds path)\n) -> torch.Tensor | tuple:\n```\n\n*Attention metadata structure:*\n\n`attn_metadata` is a **dict keyed by layer name** (`"layers.0.self_attn"`,\n`"layers.1.self_attn"`, etc.). Each attention layer indexes into it by its own\nname. The per-layer dict contains:\n\n| Key | Description |\n| --- | --- |\n| `block_table_tensor` | `[padded_num_reqs, max_blocks_per_seq]` int32 — maps (request, block_index) → physical block ID |\n| `slot_mapping` | `[total_tokens]` int64 — maps each token position → KV cache slot. Padding tokens have value `-1`. |\n| `max_query_len` | int — maximum tokens scheduled per request in this batch |\n| `block_size` | int — number of positions per KV cache block |\n| `max_blocks_per_seq` | int — max blocks allocated per sequence (equals `block_table_tensor.shape[1]`) |\n| `decode_token_threshold` | int — if `max_query_len <= decode_token_threshold`, use the decode path |', 'is_error': False}]

## USER (2026-07-21 08:13:14)

[{'tool_use_id': 'toolu_bdrk_01CBg3sbnwcYKcwztUyMtu9J', 'type': 'tool_result', 'content': '  disaggregated inference where effective context is much shorter than\n  the maximum.\n\n### Trade-offs\n\n- More buckets = slower startup (more compilations), less padding\n  waste at runtime\n- Fewer buckets = faster startup, more padding waste\n- Each bucket consumes device memory\n\n### Recommended approach\n\n1. Start with minimal buckets during development (single prefill\n   bucket, single decode batch)\n2. Profile your workload to understand prompt length and concurrency\n   distribution\n3. Add buckets matching your traffic percentiles\n4. Remove unused buckets to speed up startup\n\nFor the full parameter reference, see\n[Configuration options](reference-configuration.md#compilation-options).\n\n## Continuous batching\n\nContinuous batching is enabled by default. The Neuron scheduler\nautomatically interleaves prefill and decode requests, admitting new\nrequests without waiting for in-flight requests to complete.\n\nNo configuration is needed -- this is the default behavior when serving\nwith vLLM Neuron. For details on how the scheduler works internally,\nsee [Scheduler design](../design/vllm/neuron-scheduler.md).\n--\n## Segmented prefill\n\nSegmented prefill breaks long prompts into smaller segments, processing\nthem over multiple iterations. This enables serving long-context models\n(64K, 128K+) without compiling a single NEFF for the full sequence\nlength.\n\nSegmentation is controlled by `max_num_batched_tokens` — prompts\nexceeding this limit are processed in multiple iterations:\n\n```bash\nvllm serve openai/gpt-oss-20b \\\n    --tensor-parallel-size 8 \\\n    --max-model-len 131072 \\\n    --max-num-batched-tokens 8192\n```\n\nIn this example, a 32K prompt is processed in 4 iterations of 8192\ntokens each.\n\n:::{note}\nUnlike chunked prefill (mixed batching) in vLLM upstream, prefill and\ndecode always run in separate batches on Neuron — they are never mixed\nin the same batch.\n:::\n\n### When to use segmented prefill\n\n- Long-context models where compiling a single bucket for the full\n  context is impractical\n- Reducing peak memory during prefill by processing fewer tokens per\n  iteration\n\nFor the full design, see\n[Prefill processing design](../design/vllm/prefix-caching.md).\n\n## Prefix caching\n\nPrefix caching allows you to reuse the KV cache from shared prompt\nprefixes across requests. This improves time-to-first-token (TTFT) for\nworkloads where many requests share common system prompts or context.\n\nPrefix caching is **enabled by default** on vLLM Neuron, the same as vLLM\nupstream. You do not need to configure anything to benefit from it — requests\nthat share a prompt prefix automatically reuse the cached KV.\n\nTo disable it, pass `--no-enable-prefix-caching` (CLI) or\n`enable_prefix_caching=False` (`LLM` constructor).\n\n### Sizing the KV cache\n\nPrefix caching only helps when there are enough KV cache blocks to retain\nprefixes across requests. On Neuron, block count is set explicitly via\n`num_gpu_blocks_override`, and `block_size` must be specified:\n\n```bash\nvllm serve openai/gpt-oss-20b \\\n--\n  LM head) requires disaggregated inference — the worker rejects component DP\n  without a `--kv-transfer-config`.\n- **Vision encoder parallelism** — For multimodal models, all ranks run both the text model and the vision encoder — ranks\n  are not partitioned between them. The vision encoder has its own TP and DP\n  degrees, decoupled from the text model\'s parallelism, and only runs during\n  prefill. EP does not apply (no MoE component). By default the encoder uses\n  full DP (`tp_size=1, dp_size=world_size`) with no additional configuration.\n  To override, pass `vision_neuron_config` in `--additional-config`:\n\n  ```bash\n  vllm serve Qwen/Qwen3-VL-32B-Instruct \\\n      --tensor-parallel-size 8 \\\n      --max-model-len 8192 \\\n      --max-num-batched-tokens 8192 \\\n      --no-enable-prefix-caching \\\n      --additional-config \'{\n          "vision_neuron_config": {\n              "tp_size": 1,\n              "dp_size": 8\n          }\n      }\'\n  ```\n\n  Constraint: `tp_size * dp_size` must equal `world_size`.\n\n## Disaggregated inference\n\nDisaggregated inference separates prefill (prompt processing) and decode\n(token generation) onto different instances, allowing each phase to be\nscaled and optimized independently.\n\n### Configurations\n\n- **1P1D**: 1 prefill instance + 1 decode instance\n- **xPyD**: Multiple prefill instances + multiple decode instances for\n  higher throughput\n\n### When to use disaggregated inference\n\n- High-throughput serving where prefill and decode have different\n  resource requirements\n- Large-scale deployments where you need to scale prefill and decode\n  independently\n- Workloads with long prompts but short generations (or vice versa)\n\n## Quantization\n\nQuantization reduces model memory footprint and improves throughput by\nusing lower-precision arithmetic for inference. vLLM Neuron supports two\nmodel-weight quantization paths — FP8 static (Trn2) and MXFP4 (gpt-oss on\nTrn3) — plus FP8 KV-cache quantization. See the\n[feature/model compatibility matrix](reference-feature-model-compatibility.md)\nfor per-platform support.\n\nAlways validate with the\n[accuracy debugging guide](../model-dev/accuracy-debugging-guide.md) after\nenabling any quantization.\n\n### FP8 static weight quantization\n\nFP8 static weight quantization is driven by the **checkpoint**, not a\nruntime flag. Point the server at a ModelOpt-calibrated checkpoint carrying\nper-tensor static FP8 scales in its `quantization_config`; vLLM Neuron\ndetects the format and loads the FP8 weights automatically:\n\n```bash\nvllm serve <path-to-modelopt-fp8-checkpoint> \\\n    --tensor-parallel-size 32 \\\n--\n- [Disaggregated inference (1P1D / xPyD) tutorial](../tutorials/tutorial-di-1p1d-xpyd.md)\n  — Worked disaggregated inference deployment.', 'is_error': False}]

Your workload requires:\n\n1. **Tongyi-DeepResearch-30B-A3B** -- architecture `Qwen3MoeForCausalLM` -- a 128-expert, top-8, 30B MoE with QK-norm. No support in v0.21.0.1.0.0.\n2. **Qwen3-32B** -- architecture `Qwen3ForCausalLM` -- a dense model. No support in v0.21.0.1.0.0.\n3. **Qwen3-Embedding-8B** -- uses optimum-neuron, not vLLM. Unaffected by the plugin upgrade.\n\n---\n\n### Phase 0: Stabilize on 0.5.3 (Immediate, 0 effort)\n\n**Rationale:** Your vendored plugin is at 0.5.2 (one commit: `Release 0.5.2`). The 0.5.3 release is a trivial version bump (only GitHub workflow additions). Update the submodule pointer to 0.5.3 for consistency with the "maintenance" branch that AWS continues to support on Neuron SDK 2.31.\n\n**Actions:**\n- Update `.deps/vllm-neuron` to `origin/release-0.5.3`\n- No code changes needed; your existing `neuron_vllm_launcher.py`, compile scripts, and cluster topology remain untouched\n- This gives you a clean baseline from the "last supported NxDI release"\n\n---\n\n### Phase 1: GPT-OSS Validation on v0.21.0.1.0.0 (1-2 weeks)\n\n**Rationale:** GPT-OSS 20B/120B are the only fully-supported models in the new plugin. You already have `serve_gpt_oss_20b.bash` and `serve_gpt_oss_120b.bash`. This phase validates the new plugin\'s infrastructure on your instance without risking production models.\n\n**What changes in the stack:**\n\n| Current (0.5.x) | New (0.21.0.1.0.0) |\n|---|---|\n| `vllm==0.16.0` | `vllm==0.21.0` |\n| `neuronx-distributed-inference>=0.7` (required) | Not required (models in-plugin) |\n| `transformers 4.x` | `transformers>=5.5.1` |\n| `VLLM_NEURON_FRAMEWORK=neuronx-distributed-inference` | Not needed |\n| `--override-neuron-config \'{...}\'` (flat) | `--additional-config \'{"neuron_config": {...}}\'` |\n| `context_encoding_buckets` | `num_batched_tokens_buckets` (renamed) |\n| Manual `--num-gpu-blocks-override` | Auto-sized from HBM + `--gpu-memory-utilization` |\n| Compile via ModelBuilder thread pool monkey-patch | Plugin\'s `torch.compile` + `parallel_compile` |\n| Custom compile-only hook on `NeuronModelBase._compile_and_load_model` | `VLLM_NEURON_CPU_COMPILE=1` or normal serve (compiles automatically) |\n\n**Actions:**\n\n1. **Create a separate venv** (`.venv-neuron-v21`) with the new plugin installed from `release-0.21.0.1.0.0`\n2. **Write a new launcher script** `bash/neuron/serve_vllm_neuron_v21.bash` that:\n   - Drops `VLLM_NEURON_FRAMEWORK` entirely\n   - Uses `vllm serve` instead of `python -m vllm.entrypoints.openai.api_server`\n   - Moves `override_neuron_config` into `--additional-config \'{"neuron_config": {...}}\'`\n   - Replaces bucket field names per the migration guide\n   - Drops `NXD_COMPILE_MAX_WORKERS` (new plugin uses `VLLM_NEURON_PARALLEL_COMPILE_WORKERS` and `VLLM_NEURON_PARALLEL_TRACE_WORKERS`)\n   - Drops `--block-size` and `--num-gpu-blocks-override` (auto-sized) or keeps them only if prefix caching requires explicit block_size\n3. **Update `serve_gpt_oss_20b.bash`** to use the new launcher with:\n   ```bash\n   vllm serve openai/gpt-oss-20b \\\n       --tensor-parallel-size 8 \\\n       --max-model-len 8192 \\\n       --max-num-batched-tokens 4096 \\\n       --max-num-seqs 4\n   ```\n4. **Validate**: Confirm GPT-OSS 20B compiles and serves on 8 cores, run a few inference requests\n5. **Benchmark**: Compare TTFT and throughput against the same model on 0.5.x (if you have baselines)\n\n**What from `neuron_vllm_launcher.py` can be removed for GPT-OSS on v0.21:**\n- `limit_nxd_compile_workers()` -- NxD no longer exists; the new plugin has its own `VLLM_NEURON_PARALLEL_COMPILE_WORKERS`\n- `install_kv_quant_dtype_hook()` -- NxD\'s `KVQuantizationConfig` no longer exists\n- `install_compile_only_hook()` -- No longer hooks `NeuronModelBase._compile_and_load_model`; the new plugin compiles via `torch.compile` with its own cache\n- `install_engine_core_worker_hook()` -- The EngineCore monkey-patch for NxD thread pools is irrelevant\n- **Everything** in that file is NxD-specific. For v0.21.0.1.0.0, you will not need a custom launcher at all for supported models.\n\n---\n\n### Phase 2: Onboard Qwen3-32B Dense Model to v0.21.0.1.0.0 Plugin (3-6 weeks)\n\n**Rationale:** Qwen3-32B (`Qwen3ForCausalLM`) is architecturally a dense Llama-like model with QK-norm, SiLU, GQA. The Llama3 implementation in the new plugin is the documented porting template for dense models. Qwen3 differs mainly in:\n- QK-norm (RMSNorm on Q and K before attention)\n- Different RoPE theta (1M vs Llama\'s 500K)\n- 64 layers, 64 Q heads, 8 KV heads, head_dim=128, hidden=5120, intermediate=25600\n- Vocabulary size 151936\n\nThe Llama3 model in the new plugin already handles: segmented prefill, prefix caching, on-device sampling, EAGLE3 spec decode, various quantizations, and disaggregated inference.\n\n**Actions:**\n\n1. **Create `vllm_neuron/model/qwen3/`** in the vendored plugin with:\n   - `__init__.py` -- exports `Qwen3ForCausalLM`, `Qwen3Config`\n   - `config.py` -- dataclass mirroring `LlamaConfig` but with Qwen3 fields (qkv_bias=False, use_qk_norm=True, vocab_size=151936, etc.)\n   - `model.py` -- Fork from `llama3/model.py`, adding:\n     - QK-norm (an RMSNorm on Q and K projections after rotation)\n     - Different RoPE initialization (theta=1M, no YaRN)\n     - SiLU activation (same as Llama, no changes needed)\n   - `factory.py` -- Factory wrapping model selection\n2. **Register in `vllm_neuron/model/registry.py`:**\n   ```python\n   from .qwen3 import Qwen3ForCausalLM\n   models.append(("Qwen3ForCausalLM", Qwen3ForCausalLM))\n   ```\n3. **Write weight loaders** -- Qwen3 checkpoint format uses `model.layers.N.self_attn.{q,k,v}_proj.weight` which is the standard Llama layout. The fused QKV weight loader from the Llama model should work with minimal adaptation.\n4. **CPU smoke test** -- Use `VLLM_NEURON_CPU_MODE=1` to verify the model traces correctly on CPU before compiling on device.\n5. **Compile on Trn2** -- Start with TP=4, max_model_len=8192 (judge configuration) to validate compilation. This will exercise the new `torch.compile` pipeline.\n6. **Validate accuracy** -- Run a few prompts and compare logits against the 0.5.x NxDI-based deployment.\n7. **Update `serve_qwen3_32b_judge.bash`** to use the new plugin:\n   ```bash\n   vllm serve Qwen/Qwen3-32B \\\n       --tensor-parallel-size 4 \\\n       --max-model-len 8192 \\\n       --max-num-batched-tokens 8192 \\\n       --max-num-seqs 1\n   ```\n8. **Update `compile_qwen3_32b_judge.bash`** -- Remove systemd scope / flock complexity. The new plugin\'s compilation is automatic on first serve and cached locally/remotely via `VLLM_NEURON_REMOTE_CACHE`. May still want the flock for multi-instance coordination.\n\n**Topology impact:** The 16-replica judge cluster at TP=4 remains the same topology. The key difference is you no longer need `NEURON_RT_MULTI_INSTANCE_SHARED_WEIGHTS=TRUE` because the new plugin manages weights through its own loader.\n\n---\n\n### Phase 3: Onboard Tongyi-DeepResearch-30B-A3B (Qwen3MoE) (4-8 weeks)\n\n**Rationale:** This is the hardest piece. Tongyi (`Qwen3MoeForCausalLM`) is a 128-expert, top-8 MoE with:\n- 48 layers, 32 Q heads, 4 KV heads, head_dim=128, hidden=2048\n- Expert intermediate size 768 (small), 128 experts (many)\n- QK-norm\n- Different from GPT-OSS (32 experts, top-4, larger expert intermediate, YaRN, sliding window, no QK-norm)\n\nThe GPT-OSS model in the new plugin is the documented porting template for MoE models. It already has:\n- Expert parallelism (EP) with cross-DP token exchange\n- MoE CTE (context-to-expert) NKI kernels\n- On-device sampling, segmented prefill, prefix caching\n- MXFP4 quantization support\n\n**Actions:**\n\n1. **Create `vllm_neuron/model/qwen3_moe/`** forking from GPT-OSS:\n   - `config.py` -- Qwen3MoE-specific config (128 experts, top-8, no sliding window, QK-norm, no swiglu clamp, no attention sinks)\n   - `model.py` -- Fork GPT-OSS, adapting:\n     - Remove sliding window attention (Qwen3MoE does not use it)\n     - Remove attention sinks\n     - Add QK-norm (same as Qwen3 dense)\n     - Adjust expert routing: 128 experts, top-8 (vs GPT-OSS\'s 32 experts, top-4)\n     - Smaller expert intermediate (768 vs GPT-OSS\'s ~11K) -- affects NKI kernel tiling\n     - Remove SwiGLU clamping\n     - Different RoPE (theta=5M, no YaRN)\n   - `factory.py` -- Factory class\n2. **Register:**\n   ```python\n   from .qwen3_moe import Qwen3MoeForCausalLM\n   models.append(("Qwen3MoeForCausalLM", Qwen3MoeForCausalLM))\n   ```\n3. **EP Configuration:** With 128 experts and TP=8, you will likely use EP within TP (each rank handles 128/8=16 experts). The GPT-OSS pattern supports this natively.\n4. **Key risk: NKI kernel compatibility.** GPT-OSS\'s MoE CTE kernels are tuned for 32 experts with larger intermediates. 128 experts with 768 intermediate may need different tiling strategies. The NKI kernel selection in the new plugin should handle this via shape dispatch, but testing is essential.\n5. **Compile with production topology:** TP=8, max_model_len=128000, segmented prefill with max_num_batched_tokens=16384. This matches your current bucket configuration but expressed differently:\n   ```bash\n   vllm serve Alibaba-NLP/Tongyi-DeepResearch-30B-A3B \\\n       --tensor-parallel-size 8 \\\n       --max-model-len 128000 \\\n       --max-num-batched-tokens 16384 \\\n       --max-num-seqs 2 \\\n       --additional-config \'{\n         "neuron_config": {\n           "on_device_sampling_config": {},\n           "prefill_sequence_buckets": [16384],\n           "decode_batch_buckets": [2]\n         }\n       }\'\n   ```\n6. **Segmented prefill replaces the old bucket complexity:** The old system compiled separate NEFFs for context_encoding_buckets=[16384], prefix_buckets=[114688], token_generation_buckets=[16384,32768,...,128000]. The new system uses segmented prefill (breaks 128K into 8x16K iterations) and decode context-length bucketing. This dramatically simplifies compilation.\n7. **Prefix caching integration:** APC (Automatic Prefix Caching) is enabled by default in the new plugin. Your current system\'s prefix_buckets concept is subsumed by the native block-level prefix caching.\n\n---\n\n### Phase 4: Rewrite Compilation and Serving Scripts (2-3 weeks, overlaps with Phase 3)\n\n**What can be simplified or eliminated:**\n\n| Current Script | Disposition |\n|---|---|\n| `neuron_vllm_launcher.py` | **DELETE entirely.** All NxD patches are irrelevant. No replacement needed. |\n| `serve_vllm_neuron.bash` | **Rewrite.** Becomes a thin wrapper around `vllm serve` with standard options. Remove: VLLM_NEURON_FRAMEWORK, NXD_COMPILE_MAX_WORKERS branching, compile artifact fingerprinting (plugin handles its own cache). Keep: NEURON_RT_VISIBLE_CORES, artifact state check (optional), model source resolution. |\n| `compile_tongyi.bash` | **Simplify heavily.** The new plugin compiles automatically on first serve. For pre-compilation, use `VLLM_NEURON_CPU_COMPILE=1 vllm serve ...` or simply run a dummy request. Keep: systemd scope for memory limits, flock for mutual exclusion. Remove: ModelBuilder thread pool configuration, compile-only marker logic. |\n| `serve_tongyi.bash` | **Rewrite.** Remove NxD-specific override_neuron_config fields (save_sharded_checkpoint, blockwise_matmul_config). Map bucket configs to new field names. |\n| `serve_tongyi_cluster.bash` | **Keep structure, update inner call.** The NUMA-aware supervisor pattern, restart coordination, and embedding co-location remain valid and valuable. Just change the inner `serve_tongyi.bash` call. |\n| `serve_qwen3_32b_judge_cluster.bash` | **Same as above.** Keep the orchestration, update the inner serve call. |\n| `n_tongyi.bash` | **Keep mostly as-is.** The orchestration logic (start planning, wait, start judge, run evaluation) is decoupled from the serving layer. Minor updates to adapt to new serve scripts. |\n\n**New compilation approach:**\n\n```bash\n# Pre-compile (replaces compile_tongyi.bash)\nVLLM_NEURON_PARALLEL_COMPILE_WORKERS=16 \\\nVLLM_NEURON_COMPILATION_TIMEOUT=3600 \\\nNEURON_RT_VISIBLE_CORES=0-7 \\\nvllm serve Alibaba-NLP/Tongyi-DeepResearch-30B-A3B \\\n    --tensor-parallel-size 8 \\\n    --max-model-len 128000 \\\n    --max-num-batched-tokens 16384 \\\n    --max-num-seqs 2 \\\n    --additional-config \'{"neuron_config": {...}}\'\n# First serve compiles and caches; subsequent serves reuse cache\n```\n\nThe `VLLM_NEURON_REMOTE_CACHE` env var can point to S3 or a shared filesystem for cross-instance artifact sharing, replacing the manual `NEURON_COMPILED_ARTIFACTS` directory.\n\n---\n\n### Phase 5: Leverage New Features for Better Topology (2-4 weeks, after Phase 3)\n\n**Segmented Prefill (128K):**\n- Your current system compiles a 16K context bucket + 114K prefix bucket + multiple generation buckets. This is fragile (cold uncached suffix > 16K kills EngineCore).\n- The new system uses segmented prefill: a single 16K prefill NEFF processes any length prompt in iterations. No more prefix/context bucket combinatorics.\n- Benefit: simpler compilation, no more `PLANNING_MAX_UNCACHED_PREFILL_TOKENS` guard.\n\n**Disaggregated Inference (1P1D or xPyD):**\n- Currently you run monolithic replicas (each does both prefill and decode).\n- With disaggregated inference, you could separate:\n  - **Prefill instances** (high-throughput, batch prefill computation)\n  - **Decode instances** (latency-sensitive, continuous token generation)\n- For your planning workload (long prefill ~100K, short decode ~2K), this could dedicate more cores to prefill without blocking decode.\n- **Proposed topology:**\n  - 2 prefill replicas at TP=16 (cores 0-31) -- high prefill throughput\n  - 2 decode replicas at TP=8 (cores 32-47) -- low latency decode\n  - 1 embedding at TP=8 (cores 56-63) -- unchanged\n  - KV transfer via NIXL between prefill and decode instances\n- **Risk:** Disaggregated inference adds complexity (KV transfer config, separate compile profiles). Only pursue after stable monolithic serving.\n\n**Expert Parallelism:**\n- With 128 experts, EP can reduce per-rank memory. At TP=8 with EP=8, each rank holds 16 experts.\n- At TP=16 with EP=16, each rank holds 8 experts -- potentially better memory utilization.\n\n---\n\n### Phase 6: Update Python Infrastructure (1-2 weeks)\n\n**`planning_endpoint_pool.py`** -- **No changes needed.** This is a pure Python thread-safe routing layer that is completely decoupled from the vLLM serving implementation. It talks to endpoints via HTTP; as long as the new plugin still serves `/v1/models` and `/v1/chat/completions`, the pool works unchanged.\n\n**`neuron_embedding_server.py`** -- **No changes needed.** Uses optimum-neuron directly, not vLLM.\n\n**`PlanningEndpointRestartController`** -- **Needs minor adaptation.** The restart controller monitors `tongyi-{port}.generation` files written by the bash supervisor. As long as the supervisor bash scripts continue writing these files, no Python change is needed.\n\n**Tests:**\n- `test_neuron_vllm_launcher.py` -- **Delete.** The module it tests is being removed.\n- `test_neuron_throughput.py` -- **Keep, update imports.** If it calls vLLM directly, update to use the new API.\n\n---\n\n### Recommended Overall Sequence\n\n```\nWeek 1-2:   Phase 0 (trivial) + Phase 1 (GPT-OSS validation)\nWeek 3-5:   Phase 2 (Qwen3-32B dense model onboarding)\nWeek 4-10:  Phase 3 (Qwen3MoE / Tongyi onboarding) -- longest lead time\nWeek 6-8:   Phase 4 (script rewrites, concurrent with model work)\nWeek 9-12:  Phase 5 (new topology exploration) -- only after Phase 3 stable\nWeek 8-10:  Phase 6 (Python infrastructure cleanup)\n```\n\n**The critical path is Phase 3** -- onboarding the Tongyi MoE model. If the NKI MoE kernels in the new plugin cannot efficiently handle 128-expert top-8 routing with 768-dim intermediates, this becomes a significant development effort.\n\n---\n\n### Risk Assessment and Mitigation\n\n| Risk | Likelihood | Impact | Mitigation |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| Qwen3MoE NKI kernel incompatibility (128 experts, small intermediates) | Medium | High | Start GPU profiling early; fall back to 0.5.3 for Tongyi while Qwen3 dense migrates |\n| vLLM 0.21.0 API breaking changes in scheduler/runner | Low | Medium | Vendored plugin isolates; test early with GPT-OSS |\n| transformers v5 incompatibility with model loading | Low | Medium | Pin transformers version if needed; test in Phase 1 |\n| Segmented prefill correctness for 128K MoE | Medium | High | Validate accuracy at each segment boundary; compare with NxDI baseline |\n| Disaggregated inference adds latency for short requests | Medium | Low | Only use DI for planning (long-context); keep monolithic for judge (short-context) |\n\n---\n\n### Hybrid Strategy (If Phase 3 is Blocked)\n\nIf Tongyi MoE onboarding proves infeasible within the timeline:\n\n1. **Keep Tongyi on 0.5.3** (maintenance branch, still supported on Neuron SDK 2.31)\n2. **Migrate Qwen3-32B judge to v0.21.0** (dense model, straightforward port)\n3. **Run two venvs on the same instance:**\n   - `.venv-neuron-053` for Tongyi planning (cores 0-55)\n   - `.venv-neuron-v21` for Qwen3 judge (cores 56-63 could be reclaimed, or separate instance)\n4. **Embedding** stays on optimum-neuron (unaffected)\n\nThis hybrid approach is viable because:\n- Both plugin versions target Neuron SDK 2.31\n- Core isolation via `NEURON_RT_VISIBLE_CORES` is instance-level, not venv-level\n- The endpoint pool routes HTTP regardless of backend implementation\n\n---\n\n### Critical Files for Implementation\n\n- `/dev3/zigeng/BrowseComp-Plus/.deps/vllm-neuron/vllm_neuron/model/registry.py` (in the `release-0.21.0.1.0.0` branch) -- where new models must be registered\n- `/dev3/zigeng/BrowseComp-Plus/.deps/vllm-neuron/vllm_neuron/model/gpt_oss/model_bf16.py` (in `release-0.21.0.1.0.0`) -- MoE reference implementation to fork for Qwen3MoE\n- `/dev3/zigeng/BrowseComp-Plus/.deps/vllm-neuron/vllm_neuron/model/llama3/model.py` (in `release-0.21.0.1.0.0`) -- dense model reference implementation to fork for Qwen3-32B\n- `/dev3/zigeng/BrowseComp-Plus/bash/neuron/serve_vllm_neuron.bash` -- the central launcher that must be rewritten for the new plugin API\n- `/dev3/zigeng/BrowseComp-Plus/search_agent/neuron_vllm_launcher.py` -- to be deleted (all NxD-specific code)'}]
